<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">2012–13 Belgian Pro League</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<p>The <b>2012–13</b> season of the <b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belgian_Pro_League" title="Belgian Pro League">Belgian Pro League</a></b> (also known as <i><a href="/wiki/Jupiler" title="Jupiler">Jupiler</a> Pro League</i> for sponsorship reasons) was the 110th season of top-tier football in <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>. It started on 28 July 2012 with the first match of the regular season between <a href="/wiki/K.V._Kortrijk" title="K.V. Kortrijk">Kortrijk</a> and defending champions <a href="/wiki/R.S.C._Anderlecht" title="R.S.C. Anderlecht">Anderlecht</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schedule_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-schedule-5">[5]</a></sup> and ended on 26 May 2013, which was the return leg of the European playoff.</p>
<p>During the regular season, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Club_Brugge_K.V." title="Club Brugge K.V.">Club Brugge</a> took the early lead but then started struggling, eventually leading to the sacking of head coach <a href="/wiki/Georges_Leekens" title="Georges Leekens">Georges Leekens</a> when they dropped out of the top 6 in November. Anderlecht and overachievers <a href="/wiki/S.V._Zulte_Waregem" title="S.V. Zulte Waregem">Zulte Waregem</a> took over the top two positions and comfortably held these until the playoffs.</p>
<p>The title playoffs started with Anderlecht on 34 points and Zulte Waregem just behind them on 32. Due to the division of the points by two, they held a smaller lead over <a href="/wiki/K.R.C._Genk" title="K.R.C. Genk">Genk</a> (28 points), Club Brugge (27), <a href="/wiki/K.S.C._Lokeren_Oost-Vlaanderen" title="K.S.C. Lokeren Oost-Vlaanderen">Lokeren</a> (26) and <a href="/wiki/Standard_Li%C3%A8ge" title="Standard Liège">Standard</a> (25). To the surprise of many, Zulte Waregem took the lead about halfway through the playoffs and with Anderlecht not performing well and suffering a penalty kick trauma (missing no less than 10 penalty kicks over the course of the season and going out on penalties to Genk in the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Belgian_Cup" title="2012–13 Belgian Cup">Belgian Cup</a>), both Genk, Club Brugge and Standard Liège rapidly close the gap. Anderlecht managed to overtake Zulte Waregem again and went into the final match on 19 May 2013, at home against Zulte Waregem, with a two-point lead. Anderlecht equalized after going down 0-1 and under pressure managed to hold on, even though losing <a href="/wiki/Cheikhou_Kouyat%C3%A9" title="Cheikhou Kouyaté">Cheikhou Kouyaté</a> due to a red card. With that, Anderlecht won its 32nd title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The draw allowed Zulte Waregem to remain just in front of Club Brugge, thereby gaining access to the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>. Club Brugge and Genk qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Europa League">Europa League</a>, due to finishing 3rd and winning the Cup respectively.</p>
<p>The Europa League playoff groups were won by <a href="/wiki/K.A.A._Gent" title="K.A.A. Gent">Gent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oud-Heverlee_Leuven" title="Oud-Heverlee Leuven">Oud-Heverlee Leuven</a>, with Gent easily beating OH Leuven for the overall win. Gent had played a disappointing season, initially aiming for the top 6 but eventually finishing 12th. By winning the Europa League playoff, they won the right to play against <a href="/wiki/Standard_Li%C3%A8ge" title="Standard Liège">Standard Liège</a> for the final Europa League ticket. Gent won the first match 1-0 but lost the return 7-0, allowing Standard to take the last European ticket.</p>
<p>In the bottom end of the table, <a href="/wiki/Cercle_Brugge_K.S.V." title="Cercle Brugge K.S.V.">Cercle Brugge</a> faced a miserable season after finishing 7th the previous season, as now only three wins and five draws out of thirty matches caused them to end dead last. <a href="/wiki/Lierse_S.K." title="Lierse S.K.">Lierse</a> narrowly held of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beerschot_AC" title="Beerschot AC">Beerschot</a>, causing Cercle Brugge and Beerschot to play the relegation playoff. Beerschot initially extended their lead, but Cercle Brugge came back and on 20 April 2013, a 2-1 win by Cercle caused Beerschot to be relegated. Beerschot had been playing in the top division since <a href="/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_Belgian_First_Division" title="1989–90 Belgian First Division">1989–90</a>, initially as Germinal Ekeren, then as Germinal Beerschot. A few days after the relegation it was announced that Beerschot was in severe financial trouble and was not given a licence for professional football. On 21 May, Beerschot was officially declared bankrupt and dissolved as a whole. Cercle Brugge on the other hand, had to play the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belgian_Second_Division_Final_Rounds_2011%E2%80%9320#2013" title="Belgian Second Division Final Rounds 2011–20">Belgian Second Division Final Round</a> with second division teams <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Mouscron-P%C3%A9ruwelz" title="Royal Mouscron-Péruwelz">Mouscron-Péruwelz</a>, <a href="/wiki/K.V.C._Westerlo" title="K.V.C. Westerlo">Westerlo</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Star_Woluwe_F.C." title="White Star Woluwe F.C.">WS Woluwe</a>. On 23 May 2013, Cercle Brugge became the first team succeeding in avoiding relegation after playing the relegation playoff, since the installation of the playoffs system in <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Belgian_Pro_League" title="2009–10 Belgian Pro League">2009–10</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Teams">Teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012%E2%80%9313_Belgian_Pro_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Belgian_Pro_League" title="2011–12 Belgian Pro League">2011–12 Belgian Pro League</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K._Sint-Truidense_V.V." title="K. Sint-Truidense V.V.">Sint-Truiden</a> were relegated to the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Belgian_Second_Division" title="2012–13 Belgian Second Division">2012–13 Belgian Second Division</a> after losing their <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Belgian_Pro_League#Relegation_Playoff" title="2011–12 Belgian Pro League">relegation playoff series</a> against <a href="/wiki/K.V.C._Westerlo" title="K.V.C. Westerlo">Westerlo</a>, ending a three-season tenure in the league. Sint-Truiden were replaced by <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Belgian_Second_Division" title="2011–12 Belgian Second Division">2011–12 Second Division</a> champions <a href="/wiki/R._Charleroi_S.C." title="R. Charleroi S.C.">Charleroi</a>, who made their immediate comeback to the highest Belgian football league. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belgian_Second_Division_Final_Rounds_2011%E2%80%9320#2012" title="Belgian Second Division Final Rounds 2011–20">2012 Belgian Second Division Final Round</a>, <a href="/wiki/K.V.C._Westerlo" title="K.V.C. Westerlo">Westerlo</a> faced Second Division teams <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K._A._S._Eupen" title="K. A. S. Eupen">Eupen</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K._V._Oostende" title="K. V. Oostende">Oostende</a> and <a href="/wiki/Waasland-Beveren" title="Waasland-Beveren">Waasland-Beveren</a>. On 17 May 2012, Westerlo were relegated after a 0–0 draw away to Oostende. Also in Oostende, Waasland-Beveren secured the promotion one week later after a 1–1 draw.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadia_and_locations">Stadia and locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012%E2%80%9313_Belgian_Pro_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Stadia and locations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p><small>Source: <a class="external text" href="http://sport.be.msn.com/nl/jupilerproleague/ranking.html?comp=2639" rel="nofollow">Belgian Pro League</a><br/>
Rules for classification: 1) points; 2) number of matches won; if teams are still tied a playoff is organised<br/>
<b>(C)</b> = Champion; <b>(R)</b> = Relegated; <b>(P)</b> = Promoted; <b>(E)</b> = Eliminated; <b>(O)</b> = Play-off winner; <b>(A)</b> = Advances to a further round.<br/>
Only applicable when the season is not finished:<br/>
<b>(Q)</b> = Qualified to the phase of tournament indicated; <b>(TQ)</b> = Qualified to tournament, but not yet to the particular phase indicated; <b>(RQ)</b> = Qualified to the relegation tournament indicated; <b>(DQ)</b> = Disqualified from tournament.<br/></small></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Positions_by_round">Positions by round</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012%E2%80%9313_Belgian_Pro_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Positions by round">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Note: The classification was made after the weekend (or midweek) of each matchday, so postponed matches were only processed at the time they were played to represent the <i>real</i> evolution in standings.</p>
<p>The following matches were postponed during the season:</p>
<ul>
<li>Matchday 23: on 20 January both the match between leaders Anderlecht and second placed Zulte Waregem and the <a href="/wiki/Bruges_derby" title="Bruges derby">Bruges derby</a> between Club Brugge and Cercle Brugge were postponed due to intensive snowing. They have been rescheduled to be played end of February between matchdays 28 and 29.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ppmd23_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-ppmd23-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li>Matchday 24: also due to snow, the match between Charleroi and Cercle Brugge was postponed on 26 January. The match was played on 20 February, between matchdays 27 and 28.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ppmd24_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-ppmd24-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li>Matchday 28: yet again it was snow that prevented a match to be played. The fixture between Charleroi and Zulte Waregem was postponed on 24 February and rescheduled to 3 March, between matchdays 28 and 29.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ppmd28_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-ppmd28-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Championship_Playoff">Championship Playoff</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012%E2%80%9313_Belgian_Pro_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Championship Playoff">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The points obtained during the regular season were halved (and rounded up) before the start of the playoff. As a result, the teams started with the following points before the playoff: Anderlecht 34 points, Zulte Waregem 32, Genk 28, Club Brugge 27, Lokeren 26 and Standard 25. In the event of ties at the end of the playoffs, the half point will be deducted if it was added. Anderlecht, Genk, Lokeren and Zulte Waregem received this type of bonus due to rounding and will thus always be ranked below Club Brugge and Standard in the event of ties.</p>

Rules for classification: 1) points; 2) points after deduction of (possible) half points added due to rounding; 3) number of wins; 4) goal difference; 5) number of goals scored; 6) number of away goals scored; 7) number of away wins<br/>
<b>(C)</b> = Champion; <b>(R)</b> = Relegated; <b>(P)</b> = Promoted; <b>(E)</b> = Eliminated; <b>(O)</b> = Play-off winner; <b>(A)</b> = Advances to a further round.<br/>
Only applicable when the season is not finished:<br/>
<b>(Q)</b> = Qualified to the phase of tournament indicated; <b>(TQ)</b> = Qualified to tournament, but not yet to the particular phase indicated; <b>(RQ)</b> = Qualified to the relegation tournament indicated; <b>(DQ)</b> = Disqualified from tournament.<br/></small></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Europa_League_Playoff">Europa League Playoff</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012%E2%80%9313_Belgian_Pro_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Europa League Playoff">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Group A contains the teams finishing the regular season in positions 7, 9, 12 and 14. The teams finishing in positions 8, 10, 11 and 13 are placed in Group B.</p>

</table>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europa_League_playoff_final">Europa League playoff final</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012%E2%80%9313_Belgian_Pro_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Europa League playoff final">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The winners of both playoff groups will compete in a two-legged match to play the fourth-placed team of the championship playoff, called <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Belgian_Pro_League#Testmatches_Europa_League" title="2012–13 Belgian Pro League">Testmatch</a>. The winners of this Testmatch are granted entry to the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Europa_League#Second_qualifying_round" title="2012–13 UEFA Europa League">second qualifying round</a> of the 2012–13 UEFA Europa League.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Testmatches_Europa_League">Testmatches Europa League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012%E2%80%9313_Belgian_Pro_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Testmatches Europa League">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Relegation_Playoff">Relegation Playoff</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012%E2%80%9313_Belgian_Pro_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Relegation Playoff">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Beerschot and Cercle Brugge, the teams finishing in the last two positions, faced each other in the relegation playoff. Beerschot initially extended their three-point bonus to a six-point lead, but thereafter Cercle Brugge won three matches in a row. This caused Beerschot to be relegated to the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Second_Division" title="Belgian Second Division">Second Division</a> on 20 April 2013 after playing in the first division since 1989 (as <i>Germinal Ekeren</i> until 1999 and as <i>Germinal Beerschot</i> from 1999 until 2011). One month later however, it was announced that Beerschot had gone bankrupt and dissolved.</p>
<p>Cercle Brugge was forced to play the second division playoff with three <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Second_Division" title="Belgian Second Division">Belgian Second Division</a> teams, which they won to avoid relegation. It was the first time a team from the Pro League succeeded in surviving the Second Division Final Round since the installment of the Belgian Pro League playoffs.</p>

<p><small>Source: <a class="external text" href="http://int.soccerway.com/national/belgium/pro-league/20122013/play-offs-iii/r17995/" rel="nofollow">soccerway.com</a><br/>
Rules for classification: 1) points; 2) head-to-head points; 3) head-to-head goal difference; 4) head-to-head goals scored; 5) goal difference; 6) number of goals scored<br/>
<b>(C)</b> = Champion; <b>(R)</b> = Relegated; <b>(P)</b> = Promoted; <b>(E)</b> = Eliminated; <b>(O)</b> = Play-off winner; <b>(A)</b> = Advances to a further round.<br/>
Only applicable when the season is not finished:<br/>
<b>(Q)</b> = Qualified to the phase of tournament indicated; <b>(TQ)</b> = Qualified to tournament, but not yet to the particular phase indicated; <b>(RQ)</b> = Qualified to the relegation tournament indicated; <b>(DQ)</b> = Disqualified from tournament.<br/>
Head-to-Head: used when head-to-head record is used to rank tied teams.<br/></small></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2012%E2%80%9313_Belgian_Pro_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-notekortrijkmons-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-notekortrijkmons_43-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-notekortrijkmons_43-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">In the match between Kortrijk and Mons, Kortrijk substituted in <a href="/wiki/Brecht_Dejaegere" title="Brecht Dejaegere">Brecht Dejaegere</a> in the 89th minute while leading 3-0. As Dejaegere had not been submitted on the match sheet prior to the match, he was not allowed to play. The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Belgian_Football_Association" title="Royal Belgian Football Association">Belgian FA</a> ruled that neither team received the points, thus annulling the result and taking away three points from Kortrijk.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
